Great Elden Ring, root of the Golden Order. Anchor of all lands, giver of grace, wellspring of all joy. - The Two Fingers
The Elden Ring (エルデンリング, Eruden Ringu ) is a mysterious artifact that defines the world of Elden Ring itself. [ 1 ] It is the source of the Erdtree , [ 2 ] and its various interlocking runes represent and establish Order , the fundamental laws of the world. [ 3 ]
The Elden Ring itself is made up of various interlocking shapes, known as runes , which appear as ethereal rings and arches made of light. These runes have power over fundamental concepts that dictate reality in the Lands Between, such as "Death." Under the Golden Order, the runes represent the concepts of order and discipline enforced on the physical world. [ 4 ]
Artwork of an ancient version of the Elden Ring at Farum Azula
Long ago, the Greater Will sent a golden star bearing its vassal Elden Beast far across the cosmos to the world of the Lands Between . The beast was the living embodiment of the concept of Order , and later became the Elden Ring. [ 5 ] [ 6 ]
Special beings known as Empyreans are able to become vessels of the Elden Ring, housing it within their bodies to become gods . [ 7 ] The consort of an Empyrean takes the title of Lord, [ 8 ] and the consort of an Empyrean who has become the Elden Ring's vessel is known as an Elden Lord . The vessels can alter the runes that make up the Elden Ring itself, changing the fundamental laws of the world, as Marika did when she removed the Rune of Death and began the Age of the Erdtree . [ 9 ] The Elden Ring has taken different appearances in the past in accordance with the laws of previous ages . The oldest known configuration of the ancient Elden Ring can be found in Crumbling Farum Azula , dating to an age long before the Erdtree when Dragonlord Placidusax reigned as Elden Lord. [ 10 ]
The most recent configuration of the Elden Ring was the Golden Order , founded by its divine vessel, Queen Marika the Eternal , who later remove it from her body and shattered it with her Numen hammer . Despite her other half Radagon's attempts to repair the Ring, many of its shards scattered across the realm, the largest and most powerful of which claimed by Marika's Demigod offspring. [ 11 ] Corrupted by the strength of their newfound Great Runes , the Demigods fought a grueling Shattering War , a crucible from which no Lord arose.
Several of the runes that make up the Elden Ring have particular names. These include:
The Lands Between ( 狭間の地 , Hazama no Chi ) is the name given to the setting of Elden Ring . It is a vast realm formerly ruled by Queen Marika the Eternal .
The Lands Between is an insular landmass featuring diverse biomes, including lush southern grasslands, a temperate central region, and a frozen, mountainous north. The Erdtree dominates the skyline, its golden presence visible across most of the realm. Two great underground rivers and an enormous root system span the continent's length.
The Lands Between consists of several contrasting regions , each with its own distinct environments. They are:
It is said that long ago, the Greater Will triggered a great rupture across the heavens, [ 1 ] [ 2 ] and the vitality of the stars rained down upon the Lands Between. [ 3 ] [ 4 ] [ 5 ] [ 6 ] The first star to arrive contained the daughter of the Greater Will: Metyr, Mother of Fingers . [ 7 ] Later came a golden star bearing an Elden Beast , which later became the Elden Ring . [ 8 ]
The Lands Between witnessed the rise and fall of many civilizations and their gods . [ 9 ] [ 10 ] [ 11 ] In the prehistoric era, Dragonlord Placidusax served as the Elden Lord of the Ancient Dragons . [ 12 ] During the Age of the Erdtree , Queen Marika, vessel of the Elden Ring, [ 13 ] and her consort, the Elden Lord, ruled from Leyndell, Royal Capital, atop the Altus Plateau. Evidence of ancient cultures such as the Nox, Giants, Astrologers , Ancient Dynasty , and Hornsent remains scattered and buried throughout the realm. [ 14 ] [ 15 ] [ 16 ]
The Lands Between was also home to the Primordial Crucible , [ 17 ] [ 18 ] where all life was once blended together. [ 19 ] Under the guidance of the Two Fingers , [ 20 ] Marika transformed the Crucible into the Erdtree during her rise to power. [ 21 ] [ 22 ] She later excised the heart of the Lands Between, [ 23 ] creating a Realm of Shadow to conceal her secrets. [ 24 ]
After Marika shattered the Elden Ring, the Lands Between became the site of The Shattering : a war between her Demigod offspring. [ 25 ] Despite the power gained through their Great Runes , none of them succeeded in becoming Elden Lord. Grace was then extended to the Tarnished , [ 26 ] who were called back to the Lands Between to seek the shards of the Elden Ring, so that one may become Elden Lord. [ 27 ]
Elden Ring Nightreign is set in a parallel timeline where the Shattering War had a different outcome, featuring Limveld , a volatile and ever-changing region.
Ohh, Erdtree, great Erdtree. The Golden Order itself, unwavering, stretched to the sky. - Stranded Soul
The Erdtree (黄金樹, Ōgonju ; lit. "Golden Tree") is a giant, gold-colored tree that towers above the Lands Between in Elden Ring .
The Erdtree is the heart of the Golden Order , [ 1 ] and a divine blessing and direct product of the Elden Ring . [ 2 ] [ External 1 ] [ External 2 ] [ External 3 ]
The Altus Plateau was regarded as the realm of the Erdtree, [ 3 ] [ 4 ] and its people believed that those blessed to be born at its foot held a special significance. [ 5 ] The blessing granted by the Erdtree and consequently the Elden Ring, is represented by a golden light in the eyes of the inhabitants of the Lands Between, [ 6 ] known as the Grace of Gold . [ 7 ] Upon their deaths, the remembrances of demigods and greater champions, and other such powerful beings are hewn into the Erdtree. [ 8 ]
The entrance to the Erdtree is currently sealed by a latticework of Impenetrable Thorns in the shape of Radagon's Rune .
The Crucible of life was the primordial matter that became the Erdtree and the place where all life was once blended together. [ 9 ] [ 10 ] [ 11 ] [ 12 ] It was said to be close in nature to life itself, [ 13 ] [ 14 ] and was represented by gold with a reddish tint— primordial gold . [ 15 ] Queen Marika transformed the Crucible into the Erdtree under the guidance of the Two Fingers . [ 16 ]
Marika ushered in an Age of Plenty
The birth of the Erdtree coincided with the War Against the Giants . [ 17 ] Following the defeat of the Fire Giants and their Fell God , and the confinement of the Flame of Ruin , Queen Marika declared the beginning of a new epoch, glistening with life, known as the Age of the Erdtree. [ 18 ]
Although the Erdtree came from a blending of all life, many cultures were deemed vulgar under Marika's regime. [ 19 ] In the time of Lord Godfrey , everything once stood in opposition to the Erdtree. Through countless victories in war, it became the embodiment of Order , and defeated were eradicated, enslaved, or banished to the fringes. [ 20 ]
Amber sap dripped from the Erdtree during the age of plenty
When the new age began, the Erdtree flourished with abundance. It secreted primordial life energy in the form of sacred sap, which hardened into an amber that was treasured as the most precious of jewels. [ 21 ] These blessings fell like golden tears from its boughs, pooling in flasks or large collection basins. [ 22 ] [ 23 ] [ 24 ] Queen Marika herself personally bestowed them to her Elden Lord and chosen few. [ 25 ] [ 26 ] These Sacred Tears were worshipped and used to spread the faith in churches across all lands. [ 27 ]
During these early days, the Erdtree radiated the gentle warmth of the sun and healed all who basked in its golden glow. [ 28 ] [ 29 ] Its bark at this time was brown, [ 23 ] much like the Minor Erdtrees .
It was thought that the blessed sap of the Erdtree would drip from its boughs forever, but that era of blind belief swiftly came to an end. [ 30 ] It was only for a fleeting moment, as is the course of all life. [ 31 ] Over time, the Erdtree became more an object of faith. [ 32 ]
Heroes of the Erdtree were granted Erdtree burial
Erdtree burial was an honor awarded to heroes as a proper death meant returning to the Erdtree. [ 33 ] [ 34 ] The remains of such champions were deposited within the catacombs built around the Greattree roots that once connected to the Erdtree. [ 35 ] [ 36 ] Indeed there were once heroes abundantly blessed by the Erdtree who upon earning their honors simply died. [ 37 ] Statues of Rosus, Usher of Death , were erected in order to guide the dead who lose their way during their return to the Erdtree roots. [ 38 ]
On the Night of Black Knives , a stolen fragment of the Rune of Death was used to murder Godwyn the Golden . As a hero and the first demigod to die, Godwyn's body was buried deep beneath Leyndell in the Deeproot Depths overlooking the Nameless Eternal City . Although his soul has perished, his body did not, and his Erdtree burial enabled the Rune of Death to spread throughout the great tree roots, sprouting in the form of Deathroot across the Lands Between. [ 39 ] Deathroot violated the catacombs and gave rise to Those Who Live in Death , who refused the Erdtree's call to return. [ 40 ] At some point, either before or after the Elden Ring was shattered, the connection between the Erdtree and the great tree roots was severed. [ 35 ]
Golden Seeds were released when the Elden Ring was shattered
Minor Erdtrees were considered to be the offspring of the Erdtree. [ 41 ] After the Elden Ring was shattered, golden seeds flew from the Erdtree and scattered across the Lands Between, as if life itself knew that its end had come. [ 2 ] It used to be believed that Erdtree seeds could not exist, as the Erdtree was once perfect and eternal. [ 42 ] Erdtree Avatars emerged following the shattering of the Elden Ring, determined to protect the withering Erdtree's offspring. [ 41 ] Illusory trees, or phantom trees, also grew from the scattered golden seeds. [ 2 ] Additionally, the Wrath of Gold incantation was discovered, and feared as a sign of the Erdtree's wrath. [ 43 ]
Queen Marika was imprisoned inside the Erdtree after she shattered the Elden Ring. [ 44 ] At some point following the shattering of the Elden Ring, the entrance to the Erdtree was blocked by impenetrable thorns, emblazoned with the seal of King Consort Radagon , [ 45 ] which prevent access to anyone outside. [ 46 ] The Flame of Ruin was capable of burning the Erdtree and destroying the impenetrable thorns, but doing so was long held to be the first cardinal sin. [ 47 ]
Burning the Erdtree is the first cardinal sin
After the defeat of Morgott, the Omen King , The Tarnished attempted to enter the Erdtree to repair the Elden Ring, become Marika's consort, and ascend as Elden Lord . [ 48 ] However, they were unable to enter due to the impenetrable thorns . The Tarnished then traveled to the Mountaintops of the Giants to rekindle the Flame of Ruin and burn the Erdtree, either by sacrificing Melina (as was her duty as the kindling maiden) [ 49 ] or by using the Frenzied Flame . This journey eventually led them to Crumbling Farum Azula , where the defeat of Maliketh, the Black Blade unbound the Rune of Death, enabling them to enter the burning Erdtree.
Queen Marika was driven to the brink. The Elden Ring was broken, but by whom? And why? What could the Demigods ever hope to win by warring? - Ranni the Witch
The Shattering (破砕戦争, Hasai Sensō ) refers to the devastating and widespread war that broke out between Queen Marika the Eternal's offspring, and her demigod step-children, after the Elden Ring was shattered.
The assassination of Godwyn the Golden.
During the Golden Age of the Erdtree [ 1 ] , a fragment of the Rune of Death was stolen by Lunar Princess Ranni , who used it to forge godslaying Black Knives . [ 2 ] These knives were used by the Black Knife Assassins who, one night, entered Leyndell and assassinated Godwyn the Golden . As the assassins fled the capital, an assassin named Tiche was killed protecting her mother Alecto , the leader of the assassins.
Ranni slew body at the moment of Godwyn's death, causing the Cursemark to break into two half-wheels rather than form a circle. [ 3 ] [ 4 ] While Ranni died in the flesh, Godwyn's soul alone perished, sentencing him to live in death. [ 5 ] His body was interred in the Erdtree's roots beneath Leyndell, where it mutated and warped. Later, the Rune of Death began to spread through the roots in the form of Deathroot , giving rise to Those Who Live in Death . [ 6 ]
In preparation for the fallout of the Night of Black Knives, earlier that same night, Ranni met with her elder brother and co-conspirator, Praetor Rykard . She gifted him a slab of rock inscribed with traces of the Rune of Death, which was to serve as a last-resort foil to Maliketh, the Black Blade , in case a battle between Rykard and Maliketh came to pass.
Queen Marika shattering the Elden Ring
Radagon repairing the Elden Ring
The Night of Black Knives became the catalyst for the Shattering. [ 7 ] In response to Godwyn's death, Queen Marika the Eternal used her hammer to shatter the Elden Ring. Elden Lord Radagon , her other half, attempted to repair the Elden Ring, but in vain. [ 8 ] As punishment for her offense, Marika (alongside Radagon) was imprisoned within the Erdtree. [ 9 ]
Consequently, the shattering of the Elden Ring corrupted the Golden Order , and led to a Great War that would leave the Lands Between in ruin. [ 10 ]
The shards of the Elden Ring, known as Great Runes [ 11 ] , were inherited by Marika's Demigod offspring. [ 12 ] Tainted by the strength of the Great Runes, the Demigods warred [ 13 ] , with the conflict becoming known as the Shattering.
Morgott , a Demigod of the Golden Lineage who was born as a graceless Omen [ 14 ] , inherited a Great Rune known as the anchor ring which houses the base, proving his pedigree as a member of the Golden Lineage and as the Lord of Leyndell. [ 15 ] Taking on the moniker of the "veiled lord" [ 16 ] , Morgott ruled over Leyndell, slaughtering countless champions in defence of the Erdtree under the guise of Margit, the Fell Omen . [ 17 ]
The Blasphemous Serpent devouring Rykard
Praetor Rykard , whose noble ambitions had turned to gluttonous depravity [ 18 ] , fed himself to the blasphemous serpent after obtaining his Great Rune. [ 19 ] His consort, Tanith , established the recusants of Volcano Manor , waging a war against the Erdtree in his stead. [ 20 ]
Godrick , a distant relation of Marika whose blood was sorely diluted, [ 21 ] escaped the capital by hiding amongst the womenfolk [ 22 ] , bringing with him a multitude of treasures including the Mimic's Veil . [ 23 ] He hid from General Radahn in Stormveil Castle , and later insulted Malenia, only to grovel for mercy after he himself was defeated at her hands. [ 24 ] He turned to the act of grafting in order to attain power, so that one day he could return to the capital. [ 25 ]
Malenia and Radahn, two of the shard bearers and the most powerful demigods.
General Radahn, famed as the scourge of the stars [ 26 ] , led the Redmane Knights [ 27 ] during the Shattering. They were met in battle by Malenia, Blade of Miquella , and her undefeated army of Cleanrot Knights . [ 28 ] They fought to a standstill [ 29 ] , until Malenia unleashed her Scarlet Rot , ending the duel inconclusively. Radahn was driven mad by the rot and was forced to wander the battlefield as a mindless beast, devouring the corpses of those who died during the conflict, whether they be a friend or foe. [ 30 ] Malenia, who became comatose, was carried back to the Haligtree of her brother Miquella by Cleanrot Knight Finlay , one of the few survivors of the battle. [ 31 ]
Mohg abducting Miquella.
Ranni, the instigator of the Night of Black Knives, is said to have cast aside her Great Rune [ 32 ] , and its present whereabouts are unknown.
Mohg , known only as the Lord of Blood [ 33 ] , began building his dynasty underground in secret. [ 34 ] To this end he abducted Miquella from his resting place in the Haligtree, [ 35 ] wishing to raise the Empyrean to full godhood and become his consort. [ 36 ] However, Miquella never responded to Mohg, no matter how hard the omen tried, and continued to remain asleep in his cocoon.
Soldiers and trolls march upon the Royal Capital
The First Defense of Leyndell was precipitated by the deterioration of a sovereign alliance. [ 37 ] Godefroy the Grafted was captured by Ancient Dragon Knight Kristoff during this conflict, earning the latter the honor of Erdtree Burial. [ 38 ] The belligerents of said conflict are not confirmed; however, Godefroy's involvement may suggest that the remnants of the Golden Lineage were the attackers.
Morgott fighting General Radahn
During the Second Defense of Leyndell, Morgott, in the guise of Margit the Fell Omen, slaughtered many heroes in his defense of the Erdtree and engaged in conflict with Radahn. [ 39 ]
Whether Morgott actually defeated Radahn is unclear, as his description as the mightiest hero of the demigods would suggest not. Regardless, while the walls of Leyndell did not fall, Radahn survived, and his forces were repelled. Alongside what were apparently Radahn's forces, soldiers of Godrick and Stormveil Castle also took part in the battle [ 40 ] .
Said to have been the most appalling battle in the Shattering [ 41 ] , the conflict took place on Mt. Gelmir , seemingly between Praetor Rykard's army and the forces of Leyndell. The squalid, the sick, and the blasphemous are said to have participated in this battle, which went on without end. [ 42 ] The attackers brought the Jar Cannon to the assault; however, it was discovered that nobody knew how to use it. [ 43 ] Most of the soldiers in Leyndell's army eventually became afflicted by Frenzy and seemingly resorted to cannibalism, consuming the bodies of the dead. Rykard's own men deserted him following this conflict, no longer able to abide the consequences of his blasphemy. [ 44 ]
Godrick meeting a humiliating defeat by Malenia, Blade of Miquella.
Scarcely deserving of being considered a balanced conflict on her journey to face Radahn in the Battle of Aeonia, Malenia and her Cleanrot Knights marched past Stormveil Castle , where Godrick the Grafted and his own forces had been cowering from the Red Lion general. Apparently, Godrick did something to insult Melania, sparking a fight between the pair. Godrick was defeated, and rather than choosing to die in battle, he begged Malenia for mercy. Godrick was spared, and Malenia pressed on to meet Radahn.
Malenia and General Radahn during the Battle of Aeonia.
The final act of the Shattering was the Battle of Aeonia , a conflict between General Radahn and Malenia, Blade of Miquella. [ 45 ] It occured in the area south of Sellia, Town of Sorcery in Caelid , in a region now known as the Swamp of Aeonia . Malenia and her army of Cleanrot Knights marched southward [ 46 ] before arriving in Caelid, where they met Radahn's Redmane Knights in battle. The battle ended in a stalemate after Malenia unleashed her scarlet rot, driving the Redmane Knights to defeat. At the same time, their leader was infected with the rot, which drove Radahn into becoming a mindless beast. [ 27 ]
Ultimately, none of the Demigods succeeded in becoming Elden Lord, [ 47 ] and they were abandoned by the Greater Will . [ 48 ] [ 49 ] Instead, the guidance of Grace was extended to the Tarnished [ 50 ] , who were called to the Lands Between to claim the Great Runes, become Elden Lord, and restore the Golden Order. [ 51 ]
The Night emerging during the Shattering.
The events of the Shattering in the alternate timeline are likely the same, though the aftermath is entirely different in comparison. In the aftermath of the civil war, a primordial cataclysm known as simply the Night and its harbingers Heolstor and the Nightlords emerged and descended on the Lands Between. As Marika's shattering of the Elden Ring and the Shattering had destroyed order itself, the Night, through the Night's Tide , began plunging the Lands Between into darkness and chaos, drawing forth all manner of monsters and beasts from different realms and eras as perpetual rain threatened to wash away everything.
As the world was alternated and consumed by the Night, the Golden Order ceased to exist. Queen Marika seemed to have disappeared completely from the Lands Between, as she and the Elden Ring are no longer prayed to, though a few churches remained standing. Meanwhile, the Erdtree itself had vanished entirely from the Lands Between, and its golden, radiant hues are no longer visible. Its disappearance, along with the Grace of Gold, prevented the Tarnished from being beckoned by its call to return. The fate of many of the demigods is unknown, but they presumably died out during the Shattering, while only very few, namely Morgott, Godrick and Mohg, were left alive. In response to the growing darkness, a group of warriors from other lands known as the Nightfarers chose to stay in the Limveld to slay the Nightlords and end the Night.
Morgott and his armies consisted primarily of those who served the Erdtree , both willingly and some unwillingly.
Rykard and his forces were those who wished to oppose all the Erdtree stood for. His armies were assisted by legions of automatons like the Abductor Virgins, the Marrionettes and the Avionettes. After Rykard's transformation into the Lord of Blasphemy, almost all of his non-automaton forces abandoned him, no longer able to abide by the depravity his once rebellious ambitions had become. In their place, to support his gluttonous cause, the sacrilegious union of Rykard and the God-Devouring Serpent brought about the emergence of the Man-Serpents.
Radahn's soldiers were a revered and well trained fighting force that served their lord with unfailing loyalty. Unlike their contemporaries, Radahn's armies were very linear, in the sense they were entirely Redmane soldiers, and were supported by little to no other different forces. However, in the event of the battle of the Second Defense of Leyndell, they were apparently able to coordinate with the forces of Stormveil Castle and Godrick.
The armies of Miquella followed their lord as he parted ways with the Erdtree. They were supported by the elite Cleanrot Knights, under the command of Miquella's twin sister, Malenia. She was utterly loyal to her brother and, despite her own Empyrean selection, chose to support Miquella's ascension to godhood.
Much like the nature of their lord, the armies of Godrick the Grafted were a decentralized force of numerous warriors and creatures. Many humanoid soldiers were not organised under his banner, with large sections consisting of Exiled Soldiers and Banished Knights. Godrick also employed Kaiden Sellsword mercenaries to fight for him.
Arise now, ye Tarnished. Ye dead, who yet live. The call of long-lost grace speaks to us all. - Narrator
The Tarnished (褪せ人, Asebito ; lit. "Faded Ones/People") are a faction in Elden Ring . The player character , the Tarnished , is a member of this group.
The Tarnished are individuals who lost the grace of the Erdtree and were consequently banished from the Lands Between by Queen Marika the Eternal . Following the breaking of the Elden Ring , the Tarnished were beckoned by lost grace, fragmentary divine light from the Erdtree, to return.
In the early age of the Erdtree , Godfrey , the first Elden Lord , fought many battles throughout the Lands Between. He led the War Against the Giants , and defeated the Storm Lord . When his last enemy fell, it is said that the hue of his eyes faded. [ 1 ] Queen Marika addressed Godfrey and his warriors as she divested them of their Grace , commanding them to leave the Lands Between and travel to a faraway land , where they would wage war and die. [ 2 ] She promised them that, after their deaths, their Grace would be given back, and that they would return to the Lands Between once again, to wage war and brandish the Elden Ring. [ 3 ]
The Tarnished waged war in foreign lands
Godfrey and his kinfolk were banished from the Lands Between, beginning an exodus referred to as the Long March . [ 4 ] They left their home on boats, although one was said to have been left behind. [ 5 ] The warriors who accompanied Godfrey honored him by wielding axes , [ 6 ] although Godfrey's own axe was broken in battle during the course of the march. [ 7 ] When the Long March came to an end, Godfrey divested himself of kingship and became a simple warrior once more. [ 4 ] As Hoarah Loux, [ 8 ] he became a chieftain of the Badlands , revered by its bravest warriors. [ 9 ]
The Tarnished settled in lands outside the Lands Between, and bore descendants who were also Tarnished. [ 10 ] As Queen Marika had commanded them, the Tarnished lived and died in these distant lands.
Hoarah Loux is granted Grace once more
A long time after the Tarnished left the Lands Between, the Elden Ring was shattered and Queen Marika disappeared. [ 11 ] Marika's offspring, the Demigods , claimed shards of the Elden Ring . Tainted by their newfound strength, the Demigods warred in the Shattering , causing the Greater Will to abandon them. [ 12 ] With the war yielding no victor, the Guidance of Grace was extended to the Tarnished, who returned from the dead and went back to the Lands Between, guided by Grace. [ 13 ] [ 14 ] Upon setting foot in the Lands Between once more, the Tarnished received the aid of the Two Fingers , who bid them to seek the Great Runes possessed by the Demigods so as to restore the Golden Order and become Elden Lord . [ 15 ] The Tarnished, given life by Grace, [ 16 ] gained a form of immortality, [ 17 ] , allowing them to return from the dead over and over on their quest to become Elden Lord.
The Guidance of Grace brought together the Tarnished and their Finger Maidens , women in the service of the Two Fingers who were tasked with serving their appointed Tarnished. [ 18 ] The Finger Maidens would offer guidance and aid to the Tarnished, as well as turning the Runes they gathered into strength. [ 19 ]
The Tarnished gathered around the Table of Lost Grace
Roundtable Hold became a gathering place for the Tarnished, and was where they sought audience with the Two Fingers. [ 20 ] Among the first Tarnished to visit Roundtable Hold were Vargram the Raging Wolf [ 21 ] and Errant Sorcerer Wilhelm [ 22 ] . Vyke , a knight of the Roundtable Hold, came closer than any other Tarnished to becoming Elden Lord. However, without announcement, he disappeared below Leyndell and was scorched by the Frenzied Flame . [ 23 ] At some point, the Cursemark of Death was recovered from the body of Godwyn the Golden and taken to the Roundtable. [ 24 ] Fia, the Deathbed Companion came to the Roundtable in opposition where she siphoned the vigor of champions and developed Fia's Mist , a spell that only works against the Tarnished. [ 25 ]
Although the Tarnished had once again been given Grace, some lost sight of it once more. [ 26 ] [ 27 ] [ 28 ] At least one Tarnished, Roderika , never once saw the Guidance of Grace. [ 29 ] With many Tarnished seemingly abandoned by Grace, an Elden Lord would not arise for a long time. Roundtable Hold, once the home of venerated warriors, stopped receiving visitors. [ 30 ]
Melina assists the Tarnished who became Elden Lord
This would change when a Tarnished of no renown crossed the fog and entered the Lands Between. [ 31 ] Unlike others, this Tarnished did not meet a Finger Maiden to guide them, [ 32 ] but was instead chosen by Torrent , [ 33 ] [ 34 ] the spectral steed, and Melina , [ 35 ] a mysterious woman bound to Grace. Melina provided them with the Sacred Flasks and offered to serve as their maiden, aiding them by turning their Runes into strength. She extended an invitation to the Table of Lost Grace and bestowed the Spectral Steed Whistle to summon Torrent. [ 36 ] [ 37 ]
This Tarnished gained an audience with the Two Fingers, claimed the Great Runes, and journeyed to the Erdtree to brandish the Elden Ring and become the Elden Lord. [ 14 ]
Long ago, we began as stardust, born of a great rupture far across the skies. We, too, are children of the Greater Will. Is that not divine? Is that not sublime? - Count Ymir
The Greater Will is an unseen character in Elden Ring . It is a mysterious entity hailing from the lightless void and serving as the dominant force in Elden Ring and the history of the Lands Between . Its vassals and envoys are central to the Golden Order . Its image boosted Intelligence and Arcane . [ 1 ]
Long ago, the Greater Will fractured the One Great , creating births and souls. [ 2 ] The adherents of the Three Fingers consider this action to be a mistake, because it resulted in torment, despair, affliction, sins, and curses.
The Greater Will sent a star bearing its gleaming daughter to the Lands Between. It communicated with Metyr, Mother of Fingers , through the microcosm held between her tail fingers . [ 3 ] [ 4 ] [ 5 ] Soon, a second, golden star containing an Elden Beast arrived in the Lands Between. This Elden Beast was the Greater Will's vision for Order, and it would later become the Elden Ring . [ 6 ] This beast was its vassal, and the living incarnation of the concept of Order. [ 7 ] The Greater Will has other vassals and envoys known as the Two Fingers , [ 8 ] who speak in a cipher sign language of light . [ 9 ]
Before the age of the Erdtree , [ 10 ] the denizens of the Eternal Cities rebelled against the Greater Will. To shield themselves from its influence, the Nox donned ritual mirrorhelms to block its intervention and that of its vassals. [ 11 ] In an act of blasphemy, they drew the ire of the Greater Will by wielding the Fingerslayer Blade against one of its vassals. [ 12 ] In response to this transgression, the Greater Will unleashed Astel , whose destruction of the Eternal Cities condemned them to an existence underground. [ 13 ]
During the age of the Erdtree begun by Queen Marika the Eternal [ 14 ] and at least the era immediately preceding it, the Greater Will's envoy Two Fingers selected Empyreans as candidates to become the God of the coming age. [ 15 ] Queen Marika was one such candidate, and created the Golden Order by confining the Rune of Death . [ 16 ] However, Marika would eventually shatter the Elden Ring, [ 17 ] leading to her demigod offspring inheriting the Great Runes which in turn would trigger a war known as the Shattering . [ 18 ] The Greater Will abandoned the demigods following the Shattering, as none managed to claim title of Elden Lord. [ 19 ]
According to the Two Fingers, the Greater Will has not abandoned the realm, nor the life that inhabits it, proclaiming this is why the Tarnished have been extended the Guidance of Grace . [ 20 ] After the Tarnished returned to the Lands Between following the Shattering, the Two Fingers, at the behest of the Greater Will, bade them kill the demigods in order to claim their Great Runes to become Elden Lord by becoming Marika's consort, [ 21 ] as the Greater Will had long since renounced the demigods. [ 22 ]
In the time of The Tarnished (Protagonist) , it was discovered that the entrance to the Erdtree was blocked by impenetrable thorns, preventing anyone from becoming the Elden Lord. This caused the Two Fingers to commune with the Greater Will in search of answers, which may take thousands or tens of thousands of moons. [ 23 ] [ 24 ] When The Tarnished (Protagonist) suggested burning the Erdtree, which would unbind Destined Death and slay the world itself, [ 25 ] Finger Reader Enia exclaimed that the Fingers and the Greater Will would never allow it. [ 26 ]
After The Tarnished (Protagonist) caused the Volcano Manor's recusants to disband following the defeat of Rykard, Lord of Blasphemy , the recusant known as Knight Bernahl declared himself the inheritor of his comrade recusant's will. He declared their refusal to become the Greater Will's pawns and swore it would fall by his blade. [ 27 ]
It is not to be meddled with. It is chaos, devouring life and thought unending. - Melina
The Frenzied Flame (狂い火, Kurui Hi ), also called Yellow Flame of Frenzy (黄色い狂い火, Kiiroi Kurui Hi ) [ 1 ] [ 2 ] [ 3 ] [ 4 ] [ 5 ] and Yellow Flame of Chaos (混沌の黄色い火, Konton no Kiiroi Hi ), [ 6 ] is a force that manifests in the eyes of those stricken by maddening grief and suffering. It is feared by many for its uncanny ability to destroy individuality, capable of melting away even eternal spirits. Those deeply stricken by its folly develop an insatiable need to spread its influence further, willingly seeking to infect others with it. These afflicted, known by some as Chaos Followers , yearn for the arrival of their lord so that they may incinerate all that divides and distinguishes.
One of the unique properties of the flame, destroying individuality, manifests mainly in its ability to seemingly brainwash those it has afflicted. Many afflicted repeat the same cries and phrases despite never having interacted with one another (the most notable of these phrases being "Melt it all away..." and "May chaos take the world!" repeated ad nauseam). Seemingly blending their minds into a single, hivemind-like state.
A chosen few of those afflicted are capable of transforming into the Lord of Frenzied Flame after an apparent death, or some sort of transformation or rebirth process, it's not clearly stated and left to speculation. The strength of a lord can seemingly vary depending on who its original host was, with several individuals having proven capable of becoming one. However many of the afflicted were either too non-committal or physically feeble to accomplish anything, causing them to be considered frauds and failures in the eyes of their followers. Once a Lord of Frenzied Flame manifests, the head of the original host is replaced by a black hole with yellow flames spewing out of its core, completely erasing any trace of the original host's identity. However, if the Tarnished manages to inherit the flame, it's unclear whether his identity is truly erased. Given his ability to subdue demigods and gods like the Elden Beast, it is plausible that he did not succumb to the Flame, but instead mastered it—fusing with it rather than being consumed.
The origins of the flame are unclear, as the flame itself is said to have made its first appearance in the empty eye sockets of Shabriri , after his eyes were gouged out in punishment for slander. However, its incantations, the most powerful means that the flame manifests itself through, are also said to have come from the Three Fingers . It is also the clasp of Three Fingers that appoints a specific subject to become a Lord of Frenzied Flame.
Even without direct influence of the Three Fingers, the flame is capable of appearing on its own in sites of great suffering, such as the ninth campsite of Mt. Gelmir , where it has appeared in the eyes of Leyndell Soldiers suffering from the trauma of a particularly appalling battle. It has also appeared in the eyes of the surface-dwelling Nomadic Merchants , and while they are unable to settle and are forced to move around the lands constantly, their relative freedom gives them enough comfort to endure only minor symptoms, allowing some of them to have fairly normal conversations with passersby. They utter the mantras of the Chaos Followers only when attacked or dying.
Some have willingly pursued the Frenzied Flame in an attempt to use it as a powerful weapon, however every attempt to control the flame has ended in failure and left those who pursued it irreparably psychologically damaged. That said, even if the Tarnished chooses to purge himself from the Flame, he can still use the frenzy incantations in the pure form of a weapon, yet still susceptible to madness, however.
In a cruel twist of fate, the fear the world has for the flame has only supported its growth, as any attempt to quell it through the punishment and subjugation of its subjects has only intensified and worsened their symptoms, allowing the flame to fester more deeply into its hosts, becoming more powerful and widespread as their suffering increases. Primary example of this being the Golden Order's punishment of the Great Caravan , after they were accused of heretical beliefs, and the Hornsent's damnation of Midra and his entourage, after their attempt of studying of the flame. Both events would eventually lead to the near-or-complete successful manifestation of the Lord of Frenzied Flame .
Items related to or referencing the Frenzied Flame
Sacred spears of blood are the instruments of communion with an outer god. The mother of truth desires a wound. - Bloodfiend's Sacred Spear
The Formless Mother (姿なき母, Sugata-naki Haha ), [ 1 ] also known as Mother of Truth (真実の母, Shinjitsu no Haha ), [ 2 ] is an Outer God in Elden Ring and Shadow of the Erdtree .
The Formless Mother was encountered by Mohg deep underground. She is known to crave wounds, and to bestow power upon accursed blood . Her body can be pierced using Mohgwyn's Sacred Spear , causing the weapon to become coated in Bloodflame , or an arm can be thrust into her body in order to scatter Bloodflame on the ground, using the incantation Bloodboon .
The mother of truth offered the residents of Prospect Town salvation and transformed them into bloodfiends . [ 3 ] [ 4 ]
Verdigris is said to be the gift of an outer god. Possessed of an enormously hefty yet supple strength thanks to its rusted nature. - Verdigris Armor
The Outer Gods ( 外なる神々 , Sotonaru Kamigami ) are unseen , enigmatic entities wielding immense power and influence over the world of Elden Ring , often acting indirectly to reshape the Lands Between according to their inscrutable designs. They manifest through various natural or supernatural phenomena, often tied to one or more divine elements. [ 1 ]
The Formless Mother , also known as the Mother of Truth, is an arcane outer god associated with Omen , hornsent , [ 2 ] [ 3 ] blood , and bloodflame . [ 4 ] She craves wounds and is said to bestow power upon those born with accursed blood . [ 5 ] The Blood Oath incantations channel her divine element, [ 6 ] [ 7 ] accessed by puncturing her omnipresent body with ritual spears . [ 8 ] It is believed that the eternal blood of the Formless Mother will never dry or turn to rot. [ 9 ]
Her current followers are Mohg, the Lord of Blood ; his Mohgwyn Dynasty ; and the bloodfiends , former hornsent . [ 3 ] [ 10 ]
An outer god of Death once held influence over the Lands Between. [ 11 ] [ 12 ] Its powers presumably included Death Blight , Spectral Light , [ 13 ] and the Ghostflame wielded by the ancient Deathbirds and Gravebirds . [ 14 ] [ 15 ] This entity may also be connected to spirit -calling hexes. [ 16 ] [ 17 ] [ 18 ]
The Twinbird and White-Winged Maidens are said to be the envoys of Death. [ 19 ] After his burial at the roots of the Erdtree , Godwyn the Golden was transformed into the Prince of Death . [ 20 ] [ 21 ]
This theoretical outer god is representated by the maddening , yellow Flame of Frenzy ; [ 22 ] however, it is unclear whether the Frenzied Flame itself embodies this divinity or is simply a manifestation of its power. Nonetheless, its purpose is to catalyze the reunification of the One Great by destroying the Lands Between and plunging the world into chaos. [ 23 ] It presents profound danger to all life, [ 24 ] possessing the ability to melt away even eternal spirits . [ 25 ] The god is associated with the Eye of Yelough and contagious yellow embers in the eyes of its followers. [ 26 ] [ 27 ]
The Flame of Frenzy initially entered the world through impressions left upon the grave of an ancient god by the Readerless Fingers , likely in the Finger Ruins . [ 28 ] Later, its use was forbidden and vehemently suppressed by the Hornsent , Queen Marika , and Melina . [ 29 ] Its blind Finger Maiden later described its envoy as a "distant light," visible only after amassing numerous Shabriri Grapes . [ 30 ] [ 31 ]
The Three Fingers serve as the corporeal agents of the Frenzied Flame. Its Chaos Followers — Hyetta , Midra , Nanaya , Shabriri , Vyke , and the immured Great Caravan —await the Lord of Frenzy , who will ignite the Erdtree with the yellow flame.
An outer god of Night is thought to be the 'greater being' behind the Nightlord in Elden Ring Nightreign . [ 32 ] Its power is the Night's Tide that threatens Limveld . This god is identified by bones with a distinct lifelessness, which manifest in areas under its influence, such as the central castle and beyond the Spirit Shelter gate. The Iron Menial received one such Bone-Like Stone from the Nightlord in a dream, granting it to the Recluse when he awoke. Though it held the power to expunge divine essence, it could also be destroyed by it. [ 33 ] It also held the power to alter fate , [ 34 ] affirming a connection to the primeval current and stars . [ 35 ]
The outer god of Scarlet Rot whose essence was sealed away by a blind swordsman in the Lake of Rot . [ 37 ] [ 38 ] A great scorpion's tail, which was crafted into a dagger , is said to be a relic of this outer god. [ 39 ] Miquella's Needle was crafted and inserted into Malenia, Blade of Miquella to ward off the affliction of the Scarlet Rot. [ 22 ]
Its current followers include Romina, Saint of the Bud ; [ 40 ] Sage Gowry ; and the Servants of Rot .
According to Gowry's understanding, the Laws of an Order of Rot would be those of "Decay" (腐敗の律) and "Rebirth" (輪廻の理). [ 41 ]
This section lists the entities with a very similar role to the outer gods, but are never textually referred to as such.
The nameless god of fire is the source of the Giants' Flame and Giants' Flame incantations ; however, it interferes with the Lands Between more directly. It is an ancient, malformed deity that was depicted with curled horns and thick braids of bright red hair. [ 42 ] [ 43 ] [ 44 ] It is also tied to smithing and verdigris. [ 45 ] [ 46 ]
The blood star is a mysterious entity responsible for Briars of Punishment and Briars of Sin , two aberrant Thorn Sorceries . These sorceries require Faith to use, which implies the blood star is something that can be worshiped, and is therefore an entity. The Guilty could only see the blood star after they were blinded.
The ancient inhabitants of Mt. Gelmir made sacrifices in the name of a Serpent-God . [ 47 ] It is likely connected to one of the god-like snakes , such as the Abyssal Serpent and God-Devouring Serpent . [ 48 ]
Verdigris is said to be the gift of an outer god. Possessed of an enormously hefty yet supple strength thanks to its rusted nature. - Verdigris Armor
